  1. Beware of ordering this shaver. I needed a very particular present for a friend; I had overheard a conversation stating a portable shaver to keep in the car would be extremely desirable... I thought, &#34;Ah-hah! Present dilemma solved!&#34; Actually, finding a men's portable electric shaver was far more difficult than I would've expected. There are *approximately* 153 million males in the U.S., of which, for my proposes, I shall generously round that down to about 125 million of shaving age. Of those, let's further round it down to about 100 million who drive cars. Now, with a potential target demographic of 100 million customers, you would think the shaving companies would be a wee bit more interested than they appear to be where it comes to a portable electric shaver that you can keep & recharge in the car. Nope. Doesn't look that way. I went through all of the shavers Amazon featured (even called up Panasonic to get further details) but where portability is concerned, it appears to only center around the shaver itself and not the charger. You still need the charger to plug into the wall; no one appears to offer a car-charger cable with their shaver as-sold. After much detective work, I settled on this, the Braun Model P-70. It was obviously designed with portability in mind and was battery operated (not what I was hoping for, but I thought I'd go with it). The various reviews I read generally had very good things to say about it. It also hit more-or-less the correct price point of $124.50, so I ordered it. It arrived today and to say I was disappointed would be a huge understatement. It looked just like in the Amazon photo, but in reality it in no way had the look and feel of an item costing $125. It doesn't even come in a box, nor does it come with a travel case - it comes on a piece of cardboard with a plastic bubble over it and looks like it ought to be hanging on a hook alongside the disposable razors at your local drug store. It was shippedto me in a padded envelope. I immediately looked it up on the Amazon site and this time I noticed a blurb just below the lines of text describing the shaver's features. It stated: &#34;There is a newer version of this item.&#34; and gave a link to the &#34;Braun M90 Mobile Shaver.&#34; Wish I'd noticed that before... The M90 looks pretty much exactly like the P-70, but guess what? The price of the M90 is $21.93. That's a seriously substantial difference, wouldn't you say? I called Amazon and they confirmed to me that the price I'd paid for the P-70 was the correct price. I complained that something was 'off' with the price differential between the two items and, at this point, realized I was just going to have to return it. But now I'm in a bind big-time. I have to find a portable shaver present for my friend's birthday (tomorrow!) and I'm afraid it's not going to be easy. Not happy! If I wanted a portable shaver for myself and saw the P-70 advertised at $22 or so, I'd have been perfectly ok with it upon arrival, but not for $125! There's absolutely no way I'd give this to someone as a proper gift. If you order the P-70, you'll be wasting your money when its 'new version' costs $22! So, as I said, buyer beware.

I'm pleased with the construction of this shaver, the size and weight are nice too. It's not bulky, and it's just heavy enough to not have a chintzy feel. Feels like a solid, quality unit.   101. First of all, let me say that I got this shaver because I was tired of spending a lot of time shaving with a blade. Not only time, but also money (those blades and the shaving gel cost quite a bit, and the cost adds up overtime.) My skin was also getting irritated from shaving every morning with a razor. I decided to give this shaver a try, and have been using it for about 3 months now. Here are my impressions: The shave that you get with this machine is no worse than the result that you get with other electric shavers. It will never be as close as the shave that you can get with a razor, but it is close enough to be perfectly acceptable. As a matter of fact, this is the closest shave I have gotten from an electric razor (and I have owned 2 previous Braun shavers within the last 15 years, both of them the expensive models with rechargeable batteries.) That's not the only advantage this shaver has over other electric shavers though: This shaver uses 2 off-the-shelf AA batteries. A set of batteries lasted me for almost 2 months, which I found impressive. Since AA batteries can be found anywhere, you can use this shaver with the confidence that it will never become obsolete when its built-in battery stops being operational (which seemed to happen way too soon with the other electric shavers I owned, by the way.) So far I have used alkaline AA batteries, and at a rate of 1 set every 1 1/2 months, the cost is less than what you have to pay on blades and shaving gel. I also plan on using rechargeable batteries soon (I am not sure if this shaver works with NiMH batteries though,) which would make the cost per shave almost negligible. Another advantage is that you can use this shaver on wet skin, and can also wash it under running water. At first I was reluctant to do that, but I eventually found out that it works quite well to clean the shaver, with no ill effects. The only disadvantage to this shaver is that I believe the cutting block is not replaceable, butat the price this shaver is sold for, it would be ridiculous to spend money to replace a part that might cost almost as much as the complete machine. (Edit: After an in-depth cleaning, I verified that the cutting block is indeed replaceable, or at least removable.) Also, after more than 2 months of daily use and a serious cleaning, the shaver looks now like new. I would give it 6 stars if I could.) Yes, I like this shaver a lot. And I plan on getting a few backups.

Since it does not need any charging circuitry and has a plastic case the shaver weighs less than most. <br /> <br />- Shaves well, at least for me. I have a relatively light beard. I get as good results with the Braun 370 as I did with two previous (and much more expensive) Braun foil shavers <br /> <br />Weak points: <br />- The trimmer works, but tends to fold in on itself. It folds out at a 90 degree angle. Unless you hold the shaver parallel to where you are shaving, the trimmer will fold back into the shaver. <br /> <br />- Replacement cutting block and foil are either not available or cost twice as much as the shaver. (However I am still on my first cutting block and foil after several years' use.) <br /> <br />- Does not have the bells and whistles of \\"fancy\\" shavers - self cleaning, etc. <br /> <br />Other: <br />- Has a relatively wide shaving head, which I like. Some shavers have a muchnarrower head, which I did not like on the one like this I once had. <br /> <br /> <br />I have not compared the Pocket Twist to other shavers in a long time. There may well be ones that provide a better shave. However it has done a great job for me. <br /> <br />Even if you only use this as a travel shaver you will find it useful and very convenient.

Here's what's just ok: * Kind of noisy. * Shave was decent on my face.   255. I found this little gadget when my rotary-head Norelco razor was dropping hints of its impending demise and thought I'd pick up the Braun until I found another really good razor. I was surprised to find that the Braun 370 is a good razor. More than that, it's a really good razor. Personal items like razors have a feel that some will find more or less to their liking and some people who've grown used to a rotary-head razor might not care for this foil head on the Braun. Most differences that I expected to find annoying in this device have proved easy to get used to. First of all, this razor is much lighter and more compact than most, so it has a different heft, and it works best when held nearly perpendicular to the skin. It shaves as closely as my Norelco did, I believe, and is actually more comfortable. It has a slightly smaller shaving area and may not shave as quickly, but I don't think the difference is significant. The rotary-head Norelco was probably better at shaving a 3- or 4-day old beard, but the Braun has been perfectly fine for daily or every-other-day use. It runs on two AA batteries and I was glad to find that it works just as well on rechargeable AAs and gets about the same number of shaves on a charge that my Norelco did. Keeping a second set of batteries in my charger (or if I'm caught on a trip, dropping in a pair of disposables) means that I don't have to hunt for an electrical outlet in order to shave. The Braun has a built-in trimmer which, because of its size, I expected to be relatively useless: it's only about a half-inch wide and slides out a half-inch from the body of the shaver. The Norelco's, by contrast, was both larger and extended farther. Again, I was wrong: the Braun's trimmer is effective and easy to use and, unlike that on the Norelco, has never nicked my skin. An odd characteristic is that the trimmer slides out easily but requires a stiff push to retract. The built-in cover protects the shaving head when closed and swings open to unlock the on/off switch. It's an elegantly simple design. The razor also comes with a cleaning brush that clips into the bottom. The brush is really too small and when the shaver head is exposed, the cover blocks access to the brush; it's the only aspect of this design which seems awkward. The razor does not come with a case and probably doesn't need one. It does come with two AA alkaline batteries. I'd suggest getting a battery charger and a set of rechargeable AAs. Anyone buying this to replace an older razor might hang on to the old case and the cleaning brush as well. In short, the simple, functional design of this little razor has won me over completely; I've had it for half a year, it hasn't skipped a beat, and I still like it. Braun calls it a travel razor; right now, it's my only razor. I had no major complaints about the series of expensive razors that preceded it, but this is just, all things considered, a better razor. I have given up looking for another expensive razor and have ordered a second Braun 370 to keep in my desk at work. - - - This little gem is still available from Amazon, which surprises me, because I worry that sooner or later Braun is going to decide that it's stealing sales from the company's more expensive razors and pull it off the market. Currently, Braun calls this a model P-70 but it appears to be identical to the 370. Even the packaging is the same. (A P-70 was also a World War II aircraft but as far as I am aware, that P-70 is not available from Amazon.) It's been nearly a year since I first posted the remarks above on this razor and it's still buzzing away on rechargeable AA batteries. It hasn't missed a beat, I still like it, and it's still my only electric razor. Two additional comments: >> Braun calls this a \\"fully washable\\" travel razor. All I've ever done is remove the foil head and blow the hair out of the mechanism. I've never washed it, fully or otherwise. I've cleaned it out with the brush once or twice and once I oiled it. It still works great. >> The manufacturer probably does not intend the razor to be knocked off a counter onto a tile floor as I did once. The foil screen popped out of the shaver head and it took me nearly a minute to set the screen back on the four pins that held it in place. It still works great, but that's not an exercise I would recommend. I stand by everything I said a year ago. I've had my 370 a year and a half and it's still a great little razor.

  276. The Braun P-70 has all the inherent advantages and deficiencies of an electric shaver vs. razor blade. Have a hair the foil won't get, hit it with the trimmer. Hint: Turn the P-70 off, extend the trimmer, turn the P-70 back on. The advantage of the P-70 is that it uses AA batteries, not a built-in battery pack. You can get fresh AA's literally anywhere. Better yet, you can use rechargables.<br /><br />The weakness of ANY battery powered shaver is the decreased head speed as the battery discharges. The shaver goes from cutting the hairs, to pulling the hairs, to grabbing the hairs. Rechargables can be kept to max charge after each shave. BUT, max charge is only 1.2 volts so you are always starting slower than disposables. Until now. The new NiZn rechargable AA's are 1.6 volts (and come out of the charger at 1.85). This gives the shaver a very fast, very clean cutting speed. The blades on the head will dull and the foil over the blades will wear out with use. And the electric motor will wear out quicker with the higher voltage. I'm betting that the head and foil wear out before the motor and you have to replace the entire $18 unit anyway. This only makes economic sense if you use rechargables for all your AA needs. But, you already KNOW that you should.
